					return true;

                        } catch ( e ) {
                        	reload = false;
                        }
                    }

					// Automatically reload the page if a deprecation caused an automatic downgrade, ensure visitors get the best possible experience.
					if ( reload ) {
						location.reload();
                    }
				};

				// Suppress error alerts in older browsers
				return true;

	<h1 class="entry-header">Home page</h1>

			<div class="tabbed-nav" data-tabbed="" id="nav">
			<div class="full-width">
				<nav role="tablist">

			<div class="tab" id="tabmain" role="tabpanel">
				<h2><a href="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg" data-build-figure="inset-right"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="wp-image-84 alignright" src="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg" alt="" width="216" height="300" srcset="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg 216w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-300x417.jpg 300w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-431x600.jpg 431w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg 575w" sizes="(max-width: 216px) 100vw, 216px" /></a>Tammar wallabies</h2>
<p>Tammar wallabies (<em>Macropus eugenii</em>) are one of the smaller members of the kangaroo family, making them easy to keep in captivity and study. Typically adult males weigh 6-8 kg, whilst females weigh 5-6 kg. They are seasonal breeders and have a single young a year.</p>
<p>Tammars are a good representative of the marsupial mammals. Because they diverged from the line that led to humans and the common laboratory mammals around 150 million years ago, they make an excellent contrast. They give birth, as do all marsupials, to young at a developmental stage equivalent to an early embryo in humans, and undergo the rest of their development in the pouch. This difference in developmental timing makes them valuable for the study of development and developmental disorders.</p>

							<div class="tab" id="tab37" role="tabpanel">
				<p>The following are tools that have been included in WallaBase to use for exploring the tammar wallaby genome and associated information about it.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong><a href="http://jbrowse.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/">JBrowse</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>This is a genome browser that allows for fast visualization of genomic information, it allows users to easily visualize large datasets without the need to upload them. It supports user supplied GFF3, BED, Wiggle, BigWig, BAM, VCF and REST.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://blast.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">BLAST</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool for identifying areas of local similarity at varying evolutionary distances.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://galaxy.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">Galaxy</a></strong></li>
<li><strong><a href="http://webapollo.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">WebApollo</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool to annotate the genome in a central location. Please contact us if you are interested in using this feature.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
				</div>

            var jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade = false;

			window.onerror = function( msg, url, line, col, error ) {
				// Break out early, do not processing if a downgrade reqeust was already sent.
				if ( jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade ) {
					return true;
                }

				var xhr = new XMLHttpRequest();
				var nonce = '9a1b17ff61';
				var jQueryFunctions = [
					'andSelf',
					'browser',
					'live',
					'boxModel',
					'support.boxModel',
					'size',
					'swap',
					'clean',
					'sub',
                ];
				var match_pattern = /\)\.(.+?) is not a function/;
                var erroredFunction = msg.match( match_pattern );

                // If there was no matching functions, do not try to downgrade.
                if ( null === erroredFunction || typeof erroredFunction !== 'object' || typeof erroredFunction[1] === "undefined" || -1 === jQueryFunctions.indexOf( erroredFunction[1] ) ) {
                    return true;
                }

                // Set that we've now attempted a downgrade request.
                jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade = true;

				xhr.open( 'POST', 'https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/wp-admin/admin-ajax.php' );
				xhr.setRequestHeader( 'Content-Type', 'application/x-www-form-urlencoded' );
				xhr.onload = function () {
					var response,
                        reload = false;

					if ( 200 === xhr.status ) {
                        try {
                        	response = JSON.parse( xhr.response );

                        	reload = response.data.reload;
                        } catch ( e ) {
                        	reload = false;
                        }
                    }

					// Automatically reload the page if a deprecation caused an automatic downgrade, ensure visitors get the best possible experience.
					if ( reload ) {
						location.reload();
                    }
				};

				xhr.send( encodeURI( 'action=jquery-migrate-downgrade-version&_wpnonce=' + nonce ) );

				// Suppress error alerts in older browsers
				return true;
			}

	<h1 class="entry-header">Home page</h1>

			<div class="tabbed-nav" data-tabbed="" id="nav">
			<div class="full-width">
				<nav role="tablist">

			<div class="tab" id="tabmain" role="tabpanel">
				<h2><a href="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg" data-build-figure="inset-right"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="wp-image-84 alignright" src="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg" alt="" width="216" height="300" srcset="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg 216w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-300x417.jpg 300w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-431x600.jpg 431w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg 575w" sizes="(max-width: 216px) 100vw, 216px" /></a>Tammar wallabies</h2>
<p>Tammar wallabies (<em>Macropus eugenii</em>) are one of the smaller members of the kangaroo family, making them easy to keep in captivity and study. Typically adult males weigh 6-8 kg, whilst females weigh 5-6 kg. They are seasonal breeders and have a single young a year.</p>
<p>Tammars are a good representative of the marsupial mammals. Because they diverged from the line that led to humans and the common laboratory mammals around 150 million years ago, they make an excellent contrast. They give birth, as do all marsupials, to young at a developmental stage equivalent to an early embryo in humans, and undergo the rest of their development in the pouch. This difference in developmental timing makes them valuable for the study of development and developmental disorders.</p>
<h2>Contact</h2>
<p><a href="https://findanexpert.unimelb.edu.au/profile/12974-marilyn-renfree">Professor Marilyn Renfree</a></p>

Australia</p>

<p><a href="mailto:a.pask@unimelb.edu.au">a.pask@unimelb.edu.au</a></p>

							<div class="tab" id="tab37" role="tabpanel">
				<p>The following are tools that have been included in WallaBase to use for exploring the tammar wallaby genome and associated information about it.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong><a href="http://jbrowse.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/">JBrowse</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>This is a genome browser that allows for fast visualization of genomic information, it allows users to easily visualize large datasets without the need to upload them. It supports user supplied GFF3, BED, Wiggle, BigWig, BAM, VCF and REST.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://blast.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">BLAST</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool for identifying areas of local similarity at varying evolutionary distances.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://galaxy.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">Galaxy</a></strong></li>
<li><strong><a href="http://webapollo.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">WebApollo</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool to annotate the genome in a central location. Please contact us if you are interested in using this feature.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
				</div>

			window.onerror = function( msg, url, line, col, error ) {
				// Break out early, do not processing if a downgrade reqeust was already sent.
				if ( jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade ) {
					return true;
                }

				var xhr = new XMLHttpRequest();
				var nonce = '9a1b17ff61';
				var jQueryFunctions = [
					'andSelf',
					'browser',
					'live',
					'boxModel',
					'support.boxModel',
					'size',
					'swap',
					'clean',

                ];

                var erroredFunction = msg.match( match_pattern );

                // If there was no matching functions, do not try to downgrade.
                if ( null === erroredFunction || typeof erroredFunction !== 'object' || typeof erroredFunction[1] === "undefined" || -1 === jQueryFunctions.indexOf( erroredFunction[1] ) ) {
                    return true;

					var response,
                        reload = false;

                        	response = JSON.parse( xhr.response );

                        	reload = response.data.reload;
                        } catch ( e ) {
                        	reload = false;
                        }
                    }

					// Automatically reload the page if a deprecation caused an automatic downgrade, ensure visitors get the best possible experience.
					if ( reload ) {
						location.reload();
                    }
				};

				// Suppress error alerts in older browsers
				return true;

	<h1 class="entry-header">Home page</h1>

			<div class="tabbed-nav" data-tabbed="" id="nav">

			<div class="tab" id="tabmain" role="tabpanel">
				<h2><a href="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg" data-build-figure="inset-right"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="wp-image-84 alignright" src="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg" alt="" width="216" height="300" srcset="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg 216w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-300x417.jpg 300w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-431x600.jpg 431w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg 575w" sizes="(max-width: 216px) 100vw, 216px" /></a>Tammar wallabies</h2>
<p>Tammar wallabies (<em>Macropus eugenii</em>) are one of the smaller members of the kangaroo family, making them easy to keep in captivity and study. Typically adult males weigh 6-8 kg, whilst females weigh 5-6 kg. They are seasonal breeders and have a single young a year.</p>
<p>Tammars are a good representative of the marsupial mammals. Because they diverged from the line that led to humans and the common laboratory mammals around 150 million years ago, they make an excellent contrast. They give birth, as do all marsupials, to young at a developmental stage equivalent to an early embryo in humans, and undergo the rest of their development in the pouch. This difference in developmental timing makes them valuable for the study of development and developmental disorders.</p>

							<div class="tab" id="tab37" role="tabpanel">
				<p>The following are tools that have been included in WallaBase to use for exploring the tammar wallaby genome and associated information about it.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong><a href="http://jbrowse.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/">JBrowse</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>This is a genome browser that allows for fast visualization of genomic information, it allows users to easily visualize large datasets without the need to upload them. It supports user supplied GFF3, BED, Wiggle, BigWig, BAM, VCF and REST.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://blast.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">BLAST</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool for identifying areas of local similarity at varying evolutionary distances.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://galaxy.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">Galaxy</a></strong></li>
<li><strong><a href="http://webapollo.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">WebApollo</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool to annotate the genome in a central location. Please contact us if you are interested in using this feature.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

<h3>Annotations</h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://download.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/annotations/allMakerAnnotations.gff.gz">GFF of all Maker annotations</a></li>
<li><a href="http://download.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/annotations/fimoTFBS.gff.gz">Transcription Factor Binding Sites identified by FIMO using JASPAR</a></li>
<li><a href="http://download.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/annotations/makerGeneAnnotations.gff.gz">GFF file of Genes v3.1</a></li>
<li><a href="http://download.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/annotations/makerAnnotations.gtf.gz">GTF file of Genes v3.1</a></li>
<li><a href="http://download.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/annotations/REAPR.gff.gz">GFF file of REAPR evaluations of v3 of genome</a></li>

				if ( jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade ) {
					return true;

	<h1 class="entry-header">Home page</h1>

			<div class="tabbed-nav" data-tabbed="" id="nav">
			<div class="full-width">
				<nav role="tablist">
										<a href="#tabmain" role="tab" data-current="">
						<span class="small" data-icon="home">
							Home
						</span>
					</a>
					<a href="#tab37" role="tab">Tools</a><a href="#tab45" role="tab">Files</a>				</nav>
			</div>

			<div class="tab" id="tabmain" role="tabpanel">
				<h2><a href="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg" data-build-figure="inset-right"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="wp-image-84 alignright" src="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg" alt="" width="216" height="300" srcset="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg 216w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-300x417.jpg 300w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-431x600.jpg 431w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg 575w" sizes="(max-width: 216px) 100vw, 216px" /></a>Tammar wallabies</h2>
<p>Tammar wallabies (<em>Macropus eugenii</em>) are one of the smaller members of the kangaroo family, making them easy to keep in captivity and study. Typically adult males weigh 6-8 kg, whilst females weigh 5-6 kg. They are seasonal breeders and have a single young a year.</p>
<p>Tammars are a good representative of the marsupial mammals. Because they diverged from the line that led to humans and the common laboratory mammals around 150 million years ago, they make an excellent contrast. They give birth, as do all marsupials, to young at a developmental stage equivalent to an early embryo in humans, and undergo the rest of their development in the pouch. This difference in developmental timing makes them valuable for the study of development and developmental disorders.</p>
<h2>Contact</h2>
<p><a href="https://findanexpert.unimelb.edu.au/profile/12974-marilyn-renfree">Professor Marilyn Renfree</a></p>
<p><a href="mailto:m.renfree@unimelb.edu.au">m.renfree@unimelb.edu.au</a></p>
<p>School of BioSciences<br />
University of Melbourne<br />
Parkville<br />
Victoria 3010<br />
Australia</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><a href="https://findanexpert.unimelb.edu.au/profile/4401-andrew-pask"><strong>Professor Andrew Pask</strong></a></p>
<p><a href="mailto:a.pask@unimelb.edu.au">a.pask@unimelb.edu.au</a></p>
<p>School of BioSciences<br />
University of Melbourne<br />
Parkville<br />
Victoria 3010<br />
Australia</p>
			</div>

							<div class="tab" id="tab37" role="tabpanel">
				<p>The following are tools that have been included in WallaBase to use for exploring the tammar wallaby genome and associated information about it.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong><a href="http://jbrowse.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/">JBrowse</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>This is a genome browser that allows for fast visualization of genomic information, it allows users to easily visualize large datasets without the need to upload them. It supports user supplied GFF3, BED, Wiggle, BigWig, BAM, VCF and REST.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://blast.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">BLAST</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool for identifying areas of local similarity at varying evolutionary distances.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://galaxy.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">Galaxy</a></strong></li>
<li><strong><a href="http://webapollo.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">WebApollo</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool to annotate the genome in a central location. Please contact us if you are interested in using this feature.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
				</div>					
							<div class="tab" id="tab45" role="tabpanel">

				if ( jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade ) {
					return true;
                }

				// Break out early, do not processing if a downgrade reqeust was already sent.
				if ( jQueryMigrateHelperHasSentDowngrade ) {
					return true;
                }

				var xhr = new XMLHttpRequest();
				var nonce = '9a1b17ff61';

					'andSelf',
					'browser',
					'live',
					'boxModel',

					'size',
					'swap',

                if ( null === erroredFunction || typeof erroredFunction !== 'object' || typeof erroredFunction[1] === "undefined" || -1 === jQueryFunctions.indexOf( erroredFunction[1] ) ) {
                    return true;

                        } catch ( e ) {
                        	reload = false;

                    }

			<div class="tab" id="tabmain" role="tabpanel">
				<h2><a href="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg" data-build-figure="inset-right"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" class="wp-image-84 alignright" src="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg" alt="" width="216" height="300" srcset="https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-216x300.jpg 216w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-300x417.jpg 300w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642-431x600.jpg 431w, https://wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/files/2021/04/tammar-GS_00-0642.jpg 575w" sizes="(max-width: 216px) 100vw, 216px" /></a>Tammar wallabies</h2>
<p>Tammar wallabies (<em>Macropus eugenii</em>) are one of the smaller members of the kangaroo family, making them easy to keep in captivity and study. Typically adult males weigh 6-8 kg, whilst females weigh 5-6 kg. They are seasonal breeders and have a single young a year.</p>
<p>Tammars are a good representative of the marsupial mammals. Because they diverged from the line that led to humans and the common laboratory mammals around 150 million years ago, they make an excellent contrast. They give birth, as do all marsupials, to young at a developmental stage equivalent to an early embryo in humans, and undergo the rest of their development in the pouch. This difference in developmental timing makes them valuable for the study of development and developmental disorders.</p>

			</div>

							<div class="tab" id="tab37" role="tabpanel">
				<p>The following are tools that have been included in WallaBase to use for exploring the tammar wallaby genome and associated information about it.</p>
<ul>
<li><strong><a href="http://jbrowse.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au/">JBrowse</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>This is a genome browser that allows for fast visualization of genomic information, it allows users to easily visualize large datasets without the need to upload them. It supports user supplied GFF3, BED, Wiggle, BigWig, BAM, VCF and REST.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://blast.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">BLAST</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool for identifying areas of local similarity at varying evolutionary distances.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://galaxy.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">Galaxy</a></strong></li>
<li><strong><a href="http://webapollo.wallabase.science.unimelb.edu.au">WebApollo</a></strong>
<ul>
<li>A tool to annotate the genome in a central location. Please contact us if you are interested in using this feature.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
